font-family: AdarshaLipiExp;">fËd¡e abÉ L¢jne¡l Ó</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt 28.35pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">27.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">In view of the above, it appears that the Election Commission refused to supply the audited statements of accounts of the registered political parties to the petitioners without their opinion considering those statements as “secret information”; but it appears from Annexure-7 series to the supplementary affidavit-in-opposition filed by the respondent No.2 and the statements of paragraph No.4 to the said affidavit-in-opposition that none of the political parties specifically requested the Election Commission to consider their submitted audit statements of accounts as “confidential”.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt 28.35pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">28.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">However, citizens’ right to information has been enshrined in section 4 of the RTI Act, 2009, which runs as follows-</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt;">“Subject to the provisions of this Act, every citizen shall have the right to information from the authority, and the authority shall, on demand from a citizen, be bound to provide him with the information.”</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">29.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">As per section 8 (1) of the RTI Act any person may apply for information, which is as follows-</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt;">“Under this Act a person may apply to the officer-in-charge requesting for information either in writing or through electronic means or through e-mail.”</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">30.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">According to section 2 (f) of the RTI Act ‘<em>Information’ includes any memo, book, design, map, contract, data, log book, order, notification, document, sample, letter, report, accounts, project proposal, photograph, audio, video, drawing, painting, film, any instrument done through electronic process, machine readable record, and any other documentary material regardless of its physical form or characteristics, and any copy thereof in relation to the constitution, structure and official activities of any authority:</em></span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Provided that it shall not include note-sheets or copies of note-sheets;</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">On the other hand, in view of section 2 (b) of the RTI Act the Election Commission is an ‘authority’ and the registered political parties are required to submit their audited statements of accounts to the Election Commission under rule 9 of the Registration Rules, 2008, which runs as follows-</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyMJ;">Ò9| wbeÜ‡bi kZ©vw` cwicvjb m¤ú‡K© Kwgkb‡K AewnZKiY|- cÖ‡Z¨K wbewÜZ ivR‰bwZK `j wbeÜ‡bi kZ©vejx cwicvjb m¤ú‡K© Kwgkb‡K, mgq mgq, AewnZ Kwi‡e Ges Z`&amp;j‡¶¨ </span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ;">mswk­ó</span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyMJ;"> `j‡K wb¤œwjwLZ e¨e¯’v MªnY Kwi‡Z nB‡e, h_vt-</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .75in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyMJ; mso-fareast-font-family: SutonnyMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: SutonnyMJ;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(K)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">   </span></span></span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyMJ;">`‡ji †K›`ªxq ch©v‡q b~Zb KwgwUi wbe©vwPZ m`m¨‡`i ZvwjKv </span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ;">Ges mswk­ó</span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyMJ;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                          </span></span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .75in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyMJ; mso-fareast-font-family: SutonnyMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: SutonnyMJ;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(L)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyMJ;">`‡ji GZ`&amp;msµvšÍ mfvi Kvh©weeiYxi Abywjwc Kwgk‡b `vwLj; </span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .75in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: SutonnyMJ; mso-fareast-font-family: SutonnyMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: SutonnyMJ;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(M)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: SutonnyMJ;">cÖwZ ermi 31‡k RyjvB Gi g‡a¨ Ae¨ewnZ c~‡e©i cwÄKv erm‡ii </span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ;">mswk­ó</span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: SutonnyMJ;"> `‡ji Avw_©K †jb‡`b<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>GKwU<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>†iwRóvW© PvUvW© GKvDw›Us dvg© Øviv AwWU KivBqv AwWU wi‡cv‡U©i GKwU Kwc Kwgk‡b `vwLj;</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .75in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyMJ; mso-fareast-font-family: SutonnyMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: SutonnyMJ;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(N)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyMJ;">Kwgkb, mgq mgq, †h mKj Z_¨ ev KvMRcÎ Pvwn‡e Dnv Kwgk‡b †cÖiY; </span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: .5in; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyMJ;">Ges</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .75in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyMJ; mso-fareast-font-family: SutonnyMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: SutonnyMJ;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(O)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyMJ;">Kwgkb, mgq mgq, †h mKj wel‡qi Dci gšÍe¨ ev e¨vL¨v Pvwn‡e Dnv cwicvjb | Ó</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">31.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In view of the above provisions of law, the registered political parties are required to submit their audited statements of accounts to the Election Commission and soon after submission of such statements it falls under the category of ‘information’ as defined in the RTI Act. Moreover, soon after submission of the said audited statements it becomes “public document” under section 74 (2) of the Evidence Act, 1872. Therefore, the Election Commission being an authority under the said Act is under obligation to provide the concerned information to the petitioners.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">32.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">However, section 9(8) of the RTI Act, 2009 sets out the procedures for dealing with third-party’s “secret information” as referred to in sections 7(c), (d), (o) and (r)  of the said Act. The said provision of section 9 (8) of the RTI Act is quoted below- </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">         “Where an officer-in-charge thinks that the request made for information under sub-section (1) of section 8 is appropriate, and such information has been supplied by a third party or a third party’s interest is involved in it and the third party has considered it as secret information, the officer-in-charge shall cause a notice to be served upon the third party within 5 (five) working days for written or oral opinion, and if the third party gives any opinion in response to such notice, the officer-in-charge shall take into consideration such opinion and make a decision in respect of providing information to the applicant.”</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">33.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In the case in hand, the registered political parties did not consider their audited statements as “secret information” under sections 7(c),(d),(o) or (r) of the RTI Act; as such, in view of the said provision there was no need to seek opinion from the registered political parties for supplying their audited statements of accounts to the petitioners.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">34.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Moreover, according to the said provision, the authority from which the information has been sought is not required to rely solely on the opinion of a third-party in taking its decision; rather it shall take into consideration such opinion and arrive at a decision in accordance with the provisions of the RTI Act. As such, refusal of the Election Commission to provide with the concerned information on the ground that the political parties concerns have not provided an affirmative opinion is violative of the provisions of the said Act.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">35.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">On the other hand, section 7 of the RTI Act provides with certain types of information, which the authority is not bound to provide, and the 2<sup>nd</sup> proviso to section 7 requires that “the concerned authority shall take prior approval from the Information Commission for withholding information under this section”. But in the instant case, since the Election Commission did not seek any such prior approval from the Information Commission in respect of withholding the audited statements of accounts submitted by the political parties; hence, issuance of the impugned order is without jurisdiction and violative of the RTI Act.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">36.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In support of his submissions Mr. Sharif Bhuiyan relied on the following sets of decisions.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt 28.35pt;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">         In the case of <em>Abdul</em> <em>Momen</em> <em>vs.</em> <em>Bangladesh</em> <em>66</em> <em>DLR</em> <em>(2014)</em> <em>9,</em> the High Court Division issued a Rule Nisi calling upon the respondent Nos. (1) Bangladesh and (2) Bangladesh Election Commission to show cause as to why they should not be directed to secure to the voters particulars from the candidates for the election to the Parliament in the form of information disclosing the past of the candidates including certain facts necessary for making correct choice for candidates. In its judgment the Court held as follows:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 27.0pt;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">“….. that the Election Commission has been given a plenary power of superintendence direction and control of the preparation of the electoral rolls for elections and therefore whatever power is necessary for the purpose must be presumed to be there unless there is an ouster by express provisions.’ (Para-8)</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 27.0pt;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">‘….The respondent No.2 is further directed to disseminate the information amongst the voters about the candidates through mass media and respondent No.1 is directed to provide necessary logistic support for the purpose to the respondent No.2.” (Para-11)</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 0in 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">37.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The said decision was subsequently upheld by the Appellate Division in <em>Abu</em> <em>Safa</em> <em>vs</em>. <em>Abdul</em> <em>Momen</em> <em>Chowdhury</em> <em>66</em> <em>DLR</em> <em>(AD)</em> <em>17</em>.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 0in 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">38.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In<em> Ms. Anumeha, C/o Association for Democratic Reforms and the Chief Commissioner and Income Tax-XI , New Delhi and others,</em> the subject-matter of which case was similar to the instant matter, the Central Information Commission of India, in its decision dated 29 April, 2008, stated in paragraphs 28, 29, 45 and 49 as follows:</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 27.35pt;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">“Political parties are a unique institution of the modern Constitutional State. These are essentially civil society institutions and are, therefore, non-governmental. Their uniqueness lies in the fact that in spite of being non-governmental, political parties come to wield or directly or indirectly influence, exercise of governmental power. It is this link between State power and political parties that have assumed critical significance in the context of the Right of Information- an Act which has brought into focus the imperatives of transparency in the functioning of State institutions. It would be facetious to argue that transparency is good for all State organs, but not so good for the political parties, which control the most important of those organs. For example, it will be a fallacy to hold that transparency is good for the bureaucracy, but not good enough for the political parties which control those bureaucracies through political executives.’ (Para-28)</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 27.0pt;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">‘In modern day context, transparency and accountability are spoken of together- as twins. Higher the levels of transparency greater the accountability. This link between transparency and accountability is sharply highlighted in the Preamble to the RTI Act. -------In people’s Union for Civil Liberties (PUCL) and Ors vs. Union of India and Anr. (AIR 2003 SC 2363),  the apex court stated that it is true that the elections are fought by the political parties, yet election would be a farce if the voters are unaware of antecedents of candidates contesting elections. Their decisions to vote either in favour of ‘A’ or ‘B’ candidate would be without any basis. Such election would be neither free nor fair.----’ (Para-29)</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 27.0pt;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">“The scheme of the Act makes it abundantly clear that disclosure of information to a citizen is the norm and non-disclosure by a Public Authority an exception and it necessitates justification for any decision not to disclose an  information.’(Para-45)</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 27.0pt;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt;">‘-------The German Basic Law contains very elaborate provisions regarding political funding. Section 21 of the Basic Law enjoins that political parties shall publicly account for the sources and the use of their funds and for their assets. The German Federal Constitutional Court has in its decisions strengthened the trend towards transparency in the functioning of political parties. It follows that transparency in funding of political parties in a democracy is the norm and, must be promoted in public interest.-----” (Para-49)</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 0in 27.0pt 28.35pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">39.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In Complaints No. CIC/SM/C/2011/ 001386 and CIC/SM/C/2011/000838 filed by Shri Subhash Chandra Aggarwal and Shri Anil Bairwal respectively against the six political parties of India including Indian National Congress/ All India Congress Committee (AICC), Bharatiya Janata Party (BJP) and others, the Central Information Commission of India, in its decision dated 3<sup>rd</sup> June, 2013 stated in paragraph 77 as follows:</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt 28.35pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 27.0pt;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">“The Political Parties are the life blood of our polity. As observed by Laski ‘The life of the democratic state is built upon the party system.’ Elections are contested on party basis. The Political Parties select some problems as more urgent than others and present solutions to them which may be acceptable to the citizens. The ruling party draws its development programs on the basis of its political agenda. It is responsible for the growth and development of the society and the nation. Political Parties affect the lives of citizens, directly or indirectly, in every conceivable way and are continuously engaged in performing public duty. It is, therefore, important that they became accountable to the public.” </span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 0in 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">40.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Before passing of the Right to Information Act, 2005 in India, the Supreme Court of India upheld people’s right to access to information in relation to political parties and candidates in elections.<em> In Common Cause (A Registered Society) v. Union of India and others 2 SCC (1996) 752, </em>the following was held by the Supreme Court of India:</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 27.35pt;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">“------The political parties in their quest for power spend more than one thousand crore of rupees on the General Election (Parliament alone), yet nobody accounts for the bulk of the money so spent and there is no accountability anywhere. Nobody discloses the source of the money. There are no proper accounts and no audit. From where does the money come nobody knows. In a democracy where rule of law prevails this type of naked display of black money, by violating the mandatory provisions of law, cannot be permitted.’ (Para-18)</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 27.0pt;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">‘Superintendence and control over the conduct of election by the Election Commission include the scrutiny of all expenses incurred by a political party, a candidate or any other association or body of persons or by any individual in the course of the election. The expression “conduct of election” is wide enough to include in its sweep, the power to issue directions- in the process of the conduct of an election –to the effect that the political parties shall submit to the Election Commission, for its scrutiny, the details of the expenditure incurred or authorized by the parties in connection with the election of their respective candidates”. (Para-26)</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 0in 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">41.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In <em>Union of India v. Association for democratic Reforms and another 5 SCC (2002) 294, </em>another case decided by the Supreme Court of India before the commencement of the Right to Information Act, 2005, it was held as follows:</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 27.0pt;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">“-----After considering the relevant submissions and the reports as well as the say of the Election Commission, the High Court held that for making a right choice, it is essential that the past of the candidate should not be kept in the dark as it is not in the interest of the democracy and well being of the country. The Court directed the Election Commission to secure to voters the following information pertaining to each of the candidates contesting election to Parliament and to the State Legislatures and the parties they represent:</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; mso-list: l0 level4 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 45.0pt;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11pt;">1.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">      </span></span></em></strong><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11pt;">-----</span></em></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; mso-list: l0 level4 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 45.0pt;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11pt;">2.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">      </span></span></em></strong><em><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Assets possessed by a candidate, his or her spouse and dependent relations.</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; tab-stops: 0in 27.0pt;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt;">------.’ (Para-4)</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 107%; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 107%;">‘Thereafter, this Court in Common Cause  (A Registered Society) v. Union of India dealt with election expenses incurred by political parties and submission of return and the scope of Article 324 of the Constitution, where it  was contended that cumulative effect of the three statutory provisions, namely, Section 293-A of the Companies Act, 1956, Section 13-A of the Income Tax Act, 1961 and Section 77 of the Representation of the People Act, 1951, is to bring transparency in the election funding and the people of India must know the source of expenditure incurred by  the political parties and by the candidates in the process of election. It was contended that elections in the country are fought with the help of money power which is gathered from black sources and once elected to power, it becomes easy to collect tons of black money, which is used for retaining power and for re-election and that this vicious circle has totally polluted the basic democracy in the country. The Court held that purity <span style="letter-spacing: -0.3pt;">of election is fundamental to democracy</span> and the Commission can ask the candidates about the expenditure incurred by the candidates and by a political party for this purpose.-----’ (Para- 28 )</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">‘-----it can be deducted that the members of a democratic society should be sufficiently informed so that they may influence intelligently the decisions which may affect themselves and this would include their decision of casting votes in favour of a particular candidate. If there is a disclosure by a candidate as sought for then it would strengthen the voters in taking appropriate decision of casting their votes.’(Para-34)</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">‘If right to telecast and right to view sport games and the right to impart such information is considered to be part and parcel of Article 19(1)(a), we fail to understand why the right of a citizen /voter –a little man-to know about the antecedents of his candidate cannot be held to be a fundamental right under Article 19(1)(a). In our view, democracy cannot survive without free and fair election, without free and fairly informed voters. Votes cast by uninformed voters in favour of X or Y candidate would be meaningless. As stated in the aforesaid passage, one-sided information, disinformation misinformation and non-information, all equally create an uninformed citizenry which makes democracy a farce. Therefore, casting of a vote by a misinformed and non-informed voter or a voter having one-sided information only is bound to affect the democracy seriously. Freedom of speech and expression includes right to impart and receive information which includes freedom to hold opinions. Entertainment is implied in freedom of “speech and expression” and there is no reason to hold that freedom of speech  and expression would not cover right to get material information with regard to a candidate who is contesting election for a post which is of utmost importance in the democracy .’ (Para-38)</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">‘ The Election Commission is directed to call for information on affidavit by issuing necessary order in exercise of its power under Article 324 of the Constitution of India from each candidate seeking election to parliament or a State Legislature as a necessary part of his nomination paper, furnishing therein, information on the following aspects in relation to his/her candidature:</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">(1)-------</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">(2)-------</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">(3) The assets (immovable, movable, bank balance, etc.) of a candidate and of his/her spouse and that of dependants.</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">(4) Liabilities, if any, particularly whether there are any over dues of any public financial institution or government dues.</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">(5)-------.” (Para-48)</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 0in 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">42.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">We have gone through the aforementioned decisions and we are in respectful agreement with the ratio so decided therein. The very spirit of the said decisions in respect of the citizen’s right to information and disclosure of antecedents of candidates contesting elections and information of political parties relating to funding and candidates expenditure in election are applicable in the instant case. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">43.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In this connection it is the contention of Mr. Tawhidul Islam that the provisions of sections 7 and 9 (8) of the Right to Information Act, 2009 of Bangladesh are quite similar and identical to the provisions of sections 8 and 11 of the Right to Information Act, 2005 of India. Sections 8 and 11 of the RTI Act, 2005 of India were interpreted together by the Delhi High Court in <em>Arvind</em> <em>Kejriwal</em> <em>vs.</em> <em>Central</em> <em>Public</em> <em>Information</em> <em>Officer</em> reported in <em>AIR</em> <em>2010</em> <em>Delhi</em> <em>216</em>. In this case disclosure of information was sought to be resisted on the ground of privacy; but the Court observed (Para- 21, 22, 23, 24 and 25) that- </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level9 lfo1; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .75in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">(a)<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">   </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The procedural safeguard that has been inserted in the RTI Act intends to balance the rights of privacy and the public interest involved in disclosure of such information, and whether one should trump the other (i.e. privacy and public interest) is ultimately for the Information Officer to decide in the facts of a given case; and</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level9 lfo1; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .75in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">(b)<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">   </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The logic of section 11(1) of the RTI Act is plain; once the information seeker is provided information relating to a third-party, it is no longer in the private domain and such information seeker can then disclose in turn such information to the whole world; and  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level9 lfo1; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .75in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">(c)<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">    </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The defense of privacy cannot be lightly brushed aside; and</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level9 lfo1; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .75in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">(d)<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">   </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -0.3pt;">The competing interest (i.e. privacy</span><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"> and public interest) can possibly be weighed after undertaking hearing of all interested parties. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">44.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The above interpretation of section 11 of the Indian Act given by the Delhi High Court was again considered by a larger bench of the Delhi High Court <em>(Arvind</em> <em>Kejriwal</em> <em>vs.</em> <em>Central</em> <em>Public</em> <em>Information</em> <em>Officer)</em> on 30 September, 2011, wherein the Court after exhaustively interpreting that section observed that- (Para 5, 9, 10, 11, 12, 13, 14 and 15).</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level9 lfo1; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .75in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">(a)<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">   </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The said section 11 has to be read along with the exemptions which have been provided in section 8; and the right of the citizens to access any information held or under the control of any public authority, should be read in harmony with the exclusions /exemptions in the Act; and</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; mso-list: l0 level9 lfo1; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .75in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">(b)<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">   </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">The test which has to be applied in such conflicting interest is the larger public interest.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">45.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">The Supreme Court of India in <em>R</em>.<em>K</em>. <em>Jain</em> <em>vs.</em> <em>Union</em> <em>of</em> <em>India</em> (decided on 16 April, 2013) agreed with the above two decisions, while giving observations on the issue of disclosure of some information of ACR, which are quoted below (para-13, 14, 15 and 16):</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level9 lfo1; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .75in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">(a)<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">   </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The third-party may plead privacy defense, but such defense may, for good reasons, be overruled, in other words, after following the procedure outlined in section 11 of the RTI Act, and the authority may decide that information should be disclosed in public interest overruling any objection that the third-party may have to the disclosure; and</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level9 lfo1; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .75in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">(b)<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">   </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The disclosure must have nexus to any public activity or public interest; and</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 115%; mso-list: l0 level9 lfo1; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .75in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;">(c)<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">    </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;"> The bonafide of the applicant must be considered.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 115%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;">46.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;">The above criteria of public activity/ public interest in disclosing third-party’s information was reiterated in <em>Girigh</em> <em>Ramachandra</em> <em>Deshpande</em> <em>vs</em>. <em>Central</em> <em>Information</em> <em>Commission</em> <em>and</em> <em>others</em> (2013) 1 SCC 212.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 115%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;">47.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;">In <em>Abdul Momen Chowdhury and others vs. Bangladesh and others </em>[66 DLR (2014) 9], people’s right to know was acknowledged and disclosure and dissemination of information relating to candidates of elections to the house of nation was directed through mass media.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 115%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;">48.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;">In view of the above decisions, it is the further contention of Mr. Tawhidul Islam that the petitioners did not make out a case of larger public interest before the Election Commission or the Information Commission as against the confidentiality pleaded by the political parties for non-disclosure of the relevant information, as such no illegality was committed by the respondent No.1 in the impugned order.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">49.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">It is the admitted position of fact that the registered political parties concern did not consider their audited statements of accounts as “confidential” (as discussed herein before). On the other hand, the petitioner No.1 is the Secretary of Shushashoner Jonno Nagorik (SHUJAN), an organization which conducts various activities with a view to establishing and promoting democracy and good governance in the country by creating awareness among the citizens and ensuring their active participation. He has been involved with various activities aimed at achieving transparency, rule of law and citizens’ rights at all levels while the petitioner Nos.2 to 6 are various office-bearers of SHUJAN, who have been closely involved with various activities to promote transparency in the public life and the right of the citizens to information. As such, the above contention of Mr. Tawhidul Islam in respect of ‘confidentiality of information’ and ‘case of larger public interest’ falls through. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 115%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 0in 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;">50.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;">We have gone through the decisions of <em>Arvind</em> <em>Kejriwal</em> <em>vs.</em> <em>Central</em> <em>Public</em> <em>Information</em> <em>Officer</em> <em>AIR</em> <em>2010</em> <em>Delhi</em> <em>216</em> and <em>R</em>.<em>K</em>. <em>Jain</em> <em>vs.</em> <em>Union</em> <em>of</em> <em>India,</em> which are not applicable in the facts and circumstances of the present case, for both the decisions involved the disclosure of information relating to Annual Confidential Rolls (ACRs) of government officers, which are treated as personal information; but in the instant case, issue is disclosure of the annual audited statements of accounts of the registered political parties, which the political parties are under obligation to submit to the Election Commission according to the provision of the Registration Rules, 2008, for as soon as a political party submits such statements it becomes a “public document” (as discussed herein before). Hence, the subject matter of the instant writ petition is different from that of the above cited cases.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 115%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 0in 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;">51.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;">However, both the contesting parties relied on the decision of our jurisdiction in the case of <em>Abdul</em> <em>Momen</em> <em>vs.</em> <em>Bangladesh</em> reported in <em>66</em> <em>DLR</em> <em>(2014)</em> <em>9,</em> wherein citizen’s right to information was upheld, is applicable here in the case in hand, for the Election Commission has a similar obligation to disclose the audited statements of accounts submitted by the registered political parties concern under the Registration Rules so as to enable the public to assess the financial transparency within the political parties.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 115%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;">52.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;">In the light of the foregoing discussions and findings, the submissions made by the learned Advocate for the respondent No.2 in respect of sections 7 and 9 (8) of the RTI Act, 2009, falls through.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 115%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%; font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">         Moreover, amongst others the following objectives and purposes of the RTI Act are set out in the preamble to the said Act for establishing good governance:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 115%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 27.35pt;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;">“Whereas freedom of thought, conscience and speech is recognized in the Constitution of the People’s Republic of Bangladesh as one of the fundamental rights and right to information is an inalienable part of freedom of thought, conscience and speech; and </span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 115%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 27.0pt;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;">Whereas all powers of the Republic belong to the people, and it is necessary to ensure right to information for the empowerment of the people….”</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 115%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;">53.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;">On the other hand, the provision of section 13(5) of the RTI Act entrust the Information Commission with the positive responsibilities to preserve, promote and uphold the right of the citizens to information by, amongst other, giving effect to the principles enshrined in the Constitution of Bangladesh and making recommendation for promoting the application of the provisions of the RTI Act so as to ensure and guarantee transparency and accountability in all spheres.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 115%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;">54.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;">The impugned order is contrary to the said provision of law and hence, the same is liable to be declared without lawful authority and is of no legal effect.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 115%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 0in 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;">55.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;">In modern democratic countries citizens have a right to information in order to be able to know about the affairs of each political party which, if elected by them, seeks to formulate policies of good governance. This right to information is a basic right which the citizens of a democratic country aspire in the broader horizon of their right to live. This right has reached a new dimension and urgency, which puts better responsibility upon those political parties towards their conduct, maintenance of transparency and accountability to the public whom they aspire to represent in the parliament. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 115%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 0in 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;">56.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;">As per the provision of the Registration Rules of our country the registered political parties are required to submit their audited statements of accounts to the Election Commission every year for the purpose of, amongst others, transparency and accountability to the people and the electorate. According to the RPO, 1972 and the said Registration Rules it is the statutory duty of the Election Commission to collect such statements of accounts from those parties on an annual basis to regulate their functioning and to ensure a free and fair electoral process. As such, such statements should not be treated as ‘secret information’ under the RTI Act.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 115%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 0in 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;">57.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;">It is to be remembered, the political parties registered with the Election Commission are doing politics in the name of the people, amongst others, for the betterment of the citizens and the nation and towards establishing democracy in the country. The Central Information Commission of India in Complaints No.CIC/SM/C/2011/001386 and CIC/SM/C/2011/000838 profoundly held that <em>“The Political Parties are the life blood of our polity. As observed by Laski ‘The life of the democratic state is built upon the party system.’ Elections are contested on party basis. The Political Parties select some problems as more urgent than others and present solutions to them which may be acceptable to the citizens. The ruling party draws its development programs on the basis of its political agenda. It is responsible for the growth and development of the society and the nation. Political Parties affect the lives of citizens, directly or indirectly, in every conceivable way and are continuously engaged in performing public duty. It is, therefore, important that they became accountable to the public.”</em> </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 115%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 0in 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;">58.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;">Ignoring the people’s right to know, keeping them in dark and playing hide-and-seek with them in a democratic country like us where all powers belong to the people and their mandate is necessary for ruling the country no registered political party can be allowed to take the stand that the audited statements submitted to the Election Commission were “secret information”.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 115%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 0in 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;">59.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;">In the case in hand, though, admittedly, the political parties did not consider their submitted audited statements of accounts as ‘secret information’ or ‘confidential’, but the respondents without any mandate of law erroneously served notices upon the respective political parties concern seeking their opinion in respect of providing information to the petitioners and most of the political parties, which operate in the public sphere and have constitutional and statutory obligations for accountability and transparency, provided a negative opinion in providing such information violating the citizen’s right  to information guaranteed under the RTI Act, frustrating the purpose of the Registration Rules and the RTI Act and also damaging the spirit of ensuring and guaranteeing their transparency and accountability in all spheres including the people, which is unfortunate and hence, is deprecated.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 115%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;">60.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;">In view of the above, we find substance in the submissions made by the learned Advocate for the petitioners and merit in the Rule.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 115%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;">61.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;">In the result, the Rule is made absolute without any order as to costs.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 115%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;">62.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;">The impugned decision/order dated 16.07.2014 issued by the respondent No.1-Information Commission in Complaint No.57/2014 (Annexure-N-1) affirming the decision/order dated 22.10.2013 passed in Complaint No.97/2013 directing the respondent No.2-Election Commission to seek consent/opinion from the respective political parties with respect to disclosure of their annual audited reports to the petitioner No.1 is hereby declared to have been passed without lawful authority and is of no legal effect. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 115%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;">63.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;">Communicate this judgment at once.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 115%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;">Ed. </span></strong></span></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><a href="#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" title=""><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 10pt; line-height: 110%;">Writ Petition No. 798 of 2015</span></strong></a></span></p></div></div></div></div>
503	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Md. Ruhul Amin Howlader Vs. Mahmuda Akter Mita and another 2017 (1) LNJ 274</h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> Criminal Revision No. 1495 of 2010 </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Md. Nizamul Huq. J.</p><p><b>Court:</b> High Court Division,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Golam Mohammad Chowdhury, ,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2017 (1) LNJ 274</p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2015</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Md. Ruhul Amin Howlader </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Mahmuda Akter Mita and another</p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Criminal Law</p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2017-05-16</p><!DOCTYPE html><p><!-- [if gte mso 9]><xml>
